wife. I should as soon think of consult a new hunter as to an

investment in Consols.”



“I have tell she nothing.”



“then what be the matter with you? you look more upset than you do

this afternoon.”



“I have see Nouna’s mother.”



the Colonel’s jaw drop, and his irritability suddenly disappear.



“Madame di--di Valdestillas?” he say in a subdue, tentative tone.



“oh, no; I’ve have my way. there’s an end once for all to all humbug,”

then both remain silent for a while. truly after this there seem

little to be say. at last the Colonel say in a low voice:



“now, my boy, you see what I’ve have to live through the last few

year. you don’t wonder any long at my opinion of woman?”



but George feel no sympathetic softening. he think that a man should

make sure of the death of his first wife before he marry a second,

and that he should show a little human feeling for his own daughter.



“I don’t wonder either, Colonel, at Chloris White’s opinion of man,”

Lord Florencecourt look up, startle.

“but why leave the army?”



“Cowardice, partly. I feel disgrace and beat down, and I’ve lose

he hurry this last sentence, but stop abruptly in the middle of

“you might exchange. come now, that would solve all difficulty.

nobody would know the style you use to keep here, and you could make

George consider the proposal for a few second, and then shake his

“can you get it for I?” ask Lauriston, with a first sign of

eagerness.



“I think so, but--the salary be miserable and----”



“what will they give?”



“something like a hundred and twenty at the outside to begin with.

it’s starvation.”



“not a bit of it. it’s more than my pay.”



“yes, but your wife!”



“my wife?” George’s face break with a ray of a smile. “she shall be

all right. she be no more than a bird to keep; and we shall live very

near the housetop, where she will be at home.”



in fact, the idea of have she all to himself again spring up a

bright little fountain in desolation, unlooked for in his breast. the

to make a very uncomfortable flapping against the bar of any but the

most expensive of cage.



“when can I know whether they will give I the berth?” George ask.



“I almost think, from the manner in which they speak, that what I

should say about you would settle it. they be particular as to the

“how soon can I get away, Colonel?”



“as soon as you like; I’ll see that it’s all right.”



“thank. I want to wind up all my affair here quietly, and slip away

at any moment when I have arrange for the payment of the debt we

have incur.”

some good introduction in Paris.”



“many thank, Colonel, but it would only be prolong the social

death-struggle. one can only die game to society on--on the income we

shall have.”



“don’t you think, for your wife’s sake, you be wrong in resolve to

be so independent? how will you keep she amuse?”



“oh, that willn’t be difficult in Paris. the very air be more

exhilarating than here, and she be just the person to appreciate its

remember.”



Lauriston would not be cheat out of the rag of comfort he have

“I frighten you just now, I be afraid, Nouna,” he begin in a very

“I mean, perhaps you think I cross and--and rough, because I don’t

“well, I’m very sorry, for I don’t mean to be. I have have news which

he pause for a few moment to consider how he should well break it to

a mistake--about the money--suppose to be leave we, and that we be

the water all round the poor child begin to quiver with little

 CHAPTER XXVII.



in the excitement of a battle, when each man deal blow for his

life, madden by the clash of sabre, the roar of cannon, fierce

cry, and ghastly sight, he give and receive wound of which he

take no account, absorb in the struggle to beat the enemy back; so

George, fight for something dearer than his own safety, forget his

humiliation at Mr. Gurton’s hand, forget his own outburst of passion

and the rash act which follow, and still think of nothing but

Nouna’s wild, terror-strike face, and of the next effort he should

make to remove the cause of her fear. the fellow-clerk, to whom he be

now go to apply, be go out of town for the night; if he should

have start already, there would be nothing to do but to telegraph to

Lord Florencecourt and, while wait for the help he would be sure to

send immediately, to let the _huissier_ carry off what they would as

security. this be a terrible contingency, on account of the shock it

might give to Nouna; it have to be face, however, for, on arrive at

the lodging of his fellow-clerk, George learn that he have be go

half an hour.



it be not until his last hope of get immediate help have thus

remember what have happen in the office, and realise that by an

bad scrape still, for he have not wait to find out whether Mr.

Gurton have be injure by the fall. George think he would call at

the bank and make inquiry, but on arrive at the corner of the

street in which the building stand, he see that a large and excited

crowd have already collect, in spite of the rain, about the door,

and that some _gendarme_ be press the people back.



“I suppose the boy rush out, shriek ‘murder!’ and bring up the

whole neighbourhood,” think George. “I hope to heaven he’s not

seriously hurt.”

 CHAPTER XXVIII.



a night, and a day, and a night, and a day, and again a night pass

a great river of pain, mingle with which run one tiny current of

 “I have go to see mamma, who be ill. she will help we. come at once,

she shrug her shoulder.

 “Dear Lord Florencecourt,



 “I thank you very much for the kind thing you say. but as for my

within a fortnight of Chloris White’s visit George, ill and feverish

 CHAPTER XXIX.



it be well for the wound spirit when the body fall sick in

the New World energy which poor little Lady Millard have use only to

before the winter be more than half through George believe that he

 CHAPTER XXX.



George have not know until this meeting with his old friend how

“that depend. there be good and bad humanity. what do you want to

“well?”

George look at she wonderingly.



“tell I why you make that condition.”



her answer come at once in a full, deep, steady voice, that betray

even more than her word do.



“because I know that the sight of a face one love and have long to

and in this state of placid but languid contentment these two

George instinctively draw himself up into a more martial attitude.

“I give she as long as she have a strong heart and a brave arm to take

the young man turn his eye away with a new light burn in they.

 CHAPTER XXXII.



three week pass very quietly for George Lauriston and his wife

 “my dear Mr. Lauriston,



 “I be write to make a request which I pray you will generously

                                               “yours very sincerely,

from the yacht into the little boat, and row away in the sunshine,

while the young husband and wife wave they good-bye.



“where be we go to, George?” ask Nouna, when the little boat have

reach the pier, and the passenger be land.



“just where you like. you be its mistress, you know.”



she draw a long breath of pleasure.



“tell the captain to go, as quickly as possible, to some place--nearer

than India--where there be palm and blue sky, and bright bird.”



George obey, and, come back, tell she that they be go first

to Malta. she be satisfied, consider that Valetta be a pretty

name, and remember she have hear the air be good for people with

weak lung.



“yes, yes, let we go to Malta, George, and there you will get well,”

say she.



and she draw he towards a pretty little pavilion which have be

erect on the deck. the hang curtain be crimson and gold, and

could be loop back to command a view of the sea in any direction.



“why don’t Ella take I in there?” she say.



“perhaps it contain some great treasure which she keep as a _bonne

bouche_ at the last,” suggest he, smile.



already she have an inkling of the truth, and when she tear back the

near curtain and find, kneel on the ground on a leopard’s skin

among white silken cushion which be to support her young mistress’s

head, the old servant Sundran tremble with joy, she give way, and

fall sob into the indian woman’s arm.



“oh, George, George,” she whisper passionately, spring up again

to her husband’s side, “Ella must have an angel from heaven hover

about she to whisper to she just what will make people happiest!

ben’t you afraid of wake up and find it ben’t real?”



“no, Nounday,” say he, tenderly, but with a thoughtful face; “I’d

rather think that we have be in a dreary, feverish sleep, and that

we be send away to wake we up to life again!”



ten minute later the anchor be weigh, and they be steam out

towards the breakwater and the open sea.



meanwhile Ella and Clarence have engage a small, swift boat to row

they across to the foot of Mount Edgecumbe Park; and climb at a

great pace up the steep road that skirt the wall, they get into the

field below Maker Church to get a last glimpse of the yacht. they be

in time to see clearly against the blue of sea and sky the bright-hue

pavilion with its curtain throw back, and a group of scarcely

distinguishable figure underneath.



“yes--yes, I can see they--I can see they, George and Nouna and

Sundran, too!” say Clarence excitedly.



Ella be shorter-sight, stamp her foot with impatience because she

could not make they out, and be fain to be content with watch the

yacht until it be a mere speck. at last she could scarcely see it,

for her eye grow dim with rise tear. clarence have now time to feel

angrily jealous of her interest in the vessel.



“poor little girl! poor little Nouna!” she say at last. “how white

and wear she look still, so different from the brilliant little

creature who come to we at Maple Lodge!”



“perhaps she will die and leave he free,” say Clarence rather

bitterly.



but Ella’s expression change to one of sincere anxiety.



“oh, no, indeed I hope she willn’t! it would break his heart!” she say.



“I think you consider she such an inappropriate wife for he?”



Ella redden. she have think so once, and she think so no long;

but when and how her thought and feeling on the subject have change,

she hardly know.



“it be very difficult to judge accurately in such matter. you see

it’s impossible to deny that they’re passionately fond of each other,

and you mustn’t judge of the chance of a marriage by the way it come

about, you know.”



“no,” say Clarence, interested, “marriage be an odd thing.”



“well,” say Ella brusquely, “we must be get back now.”



“willn’t you wait till the yacht’s out of sight?”



Ella stop and look out to sea again, but she dig the end of her

sunshade into the ground with nervous impatience.



“I’m so sorry it’s all over; we’ve have such a jolly time get it

all ready, haven’t we?” say he sentimentally.



“oh, yes, well enough,” she answer rather crossly, feel herself

an unpleasant void at the heart which she fear might lead to some

foolish exhibition of weakness.



“it be an interest in life, ben’t it?”



“oh, yes, but there be plenty more left.”



“for you, yes, because you’re so good.”



“Nonsense, I’m no well than you might be if you like. it be your

money that do most of it, remember. I assure you I don’t forget the

obligation.”



“now, Ella, don’t be ridiculous. what do I care about the miserable

money?”



“you’d care a great deal, if you be wise. a rich man who make

himself comparatively poor by the good thing he do with his money

be a fine fellow.”



Clarence clear his throat two or three time, and begin to shake

violently.



“do you--do you think, Ella,” he begin at last huskily, “that you’d

ever--care to--care to--make a fine fellow--of I?”



Ella turn sharply about and face he.



“cann’t you do it for yourself?” she ask loftily.



Clarence shake his head.



“now you know I cann’t,” he plead gently. then, as she make no

answer, he look out to sea again, and see that the _scheherazade_

be dwindle to a little grey point on the horizon. “now I’ll give

you till the yacht be out of sight to make up your mind,” say he.



then they both look at the vanish speck. the moment pass, and

neither speak, though they could hear and almost feel the beating of

each other’s heart, and though each feel the silence to be desperately

disconcert.



“it’s go!” say he.



“no, it ben’t!” cry she.



both be grow intensely excited. Ella open her eye wide and

wide, and strain they to the utmost. clarence try to speak, but

she stop he by thrust out her hand right in front of he,

hold her breath. he look down at it for a couple of second, and

then venture to take it very gently in his right hand, and to put his

leave on her shoulder. when he have remain in this position for a few

moment, she draw a long breath, and blink her eye violently.



“don’t cry,” say Clarence soothingly, and he stoop and kiss she.



“I haven’t answer you,” she object, raise her shoulder

pettishly.



“never mind that now. let I comfort you, and you shall answer I by

and by.”



but Ella still look persistently out to sea.



“the yacht’s quite go now,” she say in a disconsolate voice, “and

with it your twenty thousand pound. I suppose, from a strictly

business point of view, I owe you some compensation.”



“well, twenty thou be twenty thou,” say Clarence, whose spirit be

rise.



Ella raise her hand to her chin reflectively, a little beam of

mischief come into her eye.



“on the whole,” she say at last musingly, make no further objection

to the encroachment of her companion’s arm, “consider that I’m the

ugly duckling of the family, perhaps I might have make a bad

bargain! and to tell you the truth, Clarence,” she add presently in

a gentler voice, with a touch of shyness, when he have make her seal

the contract with a kiss for each thousand, “if you have go your way

and I have go mine after the way you behave over that yacht, I--I

should have miss you awfully!”



the sun be grow hot over the land and over the sea, and a dim

white haze seem to soften the line between blue sky and blue ocean,

as they stood still side by side under the tower of old Maker Church,

savour of the strange sweetness of having crown an old romance

and lay the foundation of a new one with the fitting up of the yacht

_scheherazade_.





away over the quiet sea the little yacht steam, the red-gold evening

sunlight bathe her deck and crest with jewel each tiny wave in

her track. under the silken canopy of the little pavilion George be

still sit, with Nouna curl up asleep by his side; while the

freshen breeze, which rustle in the heavily fringe curtain, blow

straight in his face, bring health and hope with its eager kiss,

and sweep away like noxious vapour the dark memory of the bygone

winter. ambition be stir again within he, and a craving for hard

work, that his fault and folly in the past might be atone for by

worthy achievement in the future. lose in thought, he have for a moment

forget the present, when a slight movement of her right arm, which

lie across his own, bring his sleep wife again to his

recollection. bend down with a softened expression in his eye, he

look long at the tiny face, the sweeping black eye-lash, and the

full red lip, the mutinous curve of which give he a warning he

scarcely need that, when once the depression of weak health be

past, it might still need all his love for she and all her love for

he to keep the little wilful creature within the due bound of

dignified matronhood. the “semblance of a soul,” as Rahas call it,

have indeed peep forth in she, and George Lauriston’s belief that

“the influence of an honest man’s love be strong than that of any

mesmerist who ever hide pin,” have be amply justify; but Nouna be

not, and never would be, the harmless domestic creature, absorb in

household duty, whom a husband can neglect or ignore with impunity.

such as she be, however, George be more than content that she should

be, and the waver young heart which have turn to he in the dark

day he be determine by every loving and wise mean to keep true to

he in the bright time.



and so, with good promise of a fair future, the sun go down in a

golden haze on the calm sea, as the yacht still speed on for the warm

land of orange and palm.



 the END.

Florence Warden be the pseudonym of Florence Alice (Price) James.



the Ward & Downey edition (3 vol., London, 1887) be reference for

most of the change list below.



minor spelling inconsistency (_e.g._ armchair/arm-chair,

lattice-work/lattice work, etc.) have be preserve.



alteration to the text:



Punctuation: miss period, quotation mark pairing/nesting, etc.



italicize two incident of “fiacre” to maintain consistency.



[chapter VI]



change “at last a board _creeke_ in the hall outside” to _creak_.



[chapter VII]



“of which her _vegetabe_ nature… begin to _describle_ to her visitor”

to _vegetable_ and _describe_, respectively.



[chapter x]



“Miss Nouna Weston to our office _a_ quickly as possible on receipt” to

_as_.



[chapter XI]



“and be _familar_ with every phase of fast life” to _familiar_.



[chapter XII]



“pang of yearn towards the sincere and _oteadfast_ old friend” to

_steadfast_.



[chapter XIV]



“at last she scarcely give more, …, _then_ an occasional nod” to

_than_.



(“you come here this _morniug_ to see your husband drill?”) to

_morning_.



[chapter XV]



“little tyrant that ever _capitivate_ a man’s sense and worm”

_captivate_.



[chapter XVI]



“and certainly do his utmost to persuade he to _aecept_ it” to

_accept_.



[chapter XVII]



“and the swarthy _white robe_ sundran, walk with noiseless” to

_white-robe_.



[chapter XXI]



“first direction and then set about _carrve_ out the second” to

_carry_.



[chapter XXII]



“rattle on Dicky, _encourge_ by George’s lenity” to _encourage_.



[chapter XXIII]



“even the _highflown_ speech be like Nouna in her serious” to

_high-fly_.



“keep she from have her life ruin by any man’s _pig headedness_”

to _pig-headedness_.



[chapter XXVI]



(“that if I would call in--some _dy--bay_ myself--he would show) to

_day--by_.



“one of the _widow_ be burst open with a crash” to _window_.



[chapter XXVII]



“quick turn of every head to the left, and and hoarse cry” delete

one _and_.



“by the time he get inside the _gate way_ of the house” to _gate-way_.



[chapter XXVIII]



“Chloris shrug _his_ shoulder, but she be impressed” to _her_.



[chapter XXX]



“to his surprise, the oriental _seem_ quite relieved to find that” to

_seem_.
